## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science & solid mechanics (thermomechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the standard setting for constitutive laws of solids/metals/polymers capturing elastic response, plastic strain hardening, and temperature-dependent softening/thermal expansion effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelasticity (Hooke + thermal strain): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (small-strain elastic solid with coefficient of thermal expansion and stress-free temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus varies approximately linearly with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential softening): sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) * epsilon (modulus decreases with temperature, common near softening regimes)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial (Murnaghan/Landau-type 1D expansion): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon^2 (weak nonlinearity in elasticity with thermal dependence)
- Ramberg–Osgood (compliance form, implicit): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * (sigma^(c2)) (elastic + nonlinear plastic strain; used for metals in monotonic loading)
- Ludwik/Hollomon strain hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon^(c2)) * exp(-c3 * T) (power-law hardening multiplied by a temperature softening factor)
- Voce hardening (saturating flow stress): sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon)) * exp(-c3 * T) (hardening saturates at large strain; softened by temperature)
- Johnson–Cook-like (no strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon^(c2)) * (1 - c3 * (T - c4)^(c5)) (metal plasticity with thermal softening relative to a reference temperature)
- Hyperbolic-sine hardening (Eyring/thermal activation-inspired): sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(-c2 * T) (captures transition from linear to logarithmic-like growth with thermal effects)
- Elastic–perfectly plastic (smooth approximation): sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(-c2 * T) (approximates yield/plateau behavior without explicit piecewise definitions)
- Thermoelastic stress offset (residual/thermal mismatch): sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon - c2 * T (baseline stress plus mechanical term minus thermal term; simplified linear coupling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If sigma is approximately linear in epsilon at fixed T, prefer sigma ≈ E(T) * epsilon with E(T) slowly varying (linear or exponential in T).
- If curves at different T are roughly parallel but shifted along epsilon, model a stress-free thermal strain: replace epsilon by (epsilon - alpha*(T-T0)).
- If sigma increases rapidly at small epsilon and then approaches a limiting slope or plateau, use saturating hardening forms (Voce-type: 1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or tanh-like smooth yield.
- If higher T uniformly lowers sigma across epsilon (softening), use multiplicative softening factors such as exp(-c*T) or (1 - c*(T-T0)^m) multiplying an epsilon-dependent backbone.
- If hardening is approximately a straight line on log(sigma) vs log(epsilon), use power-law hardening sigma ∝ epsilon^n (possibly with T-dependent prefactor).
- If sigma shows an initially linear region followed by strong curvature, use additive elastic + plastic strain decompositions (Ramberg–Osgood implicit structure).
- If temperature sensitivity grows at larger strain (e.g., more softening at high epsilon), include coupled terms like exp(-c*T) * epsilon^n or (c0 + c1*T)*epsilon + (c2 + c3*T)*epsilon^2 rather than separable E(T)*epsilon alone.
- If sigma vs T at fixed epsilon is roughly linear over the data range, a bilinear coupling sigma = a0 + a1*epsilon + a2*T + a3*epsilon*T is often sufficient before introducing exponentials.

GT (fixed):  
\[
-0.6056800229\,(T-298.0016449)\;+\;\epsilon\cdot 3.1473717381\cdot e^{-(T-298.0016449)^2}
\]
So GT is **(i)** affine in \(T\) plus **(ii)** a term **linear in \(\epsilon\)** whose coefficient is a **Gaussian in \(T\)** centered at \(298.0016\) with exponent \(-(T-c)^2\). No other \(\epsilon\)-dependence exists.

A candidate can match only if, after choosing its constants (and possibly restricting to a plausible domain), it can produce:
- a linear-in-\(T\) baseline with slope \(-0.60568...\) and intercept \(0.60568...\cdot 298.0016...\),
- plus an \(\epsilon\) term whose \(T\)-dependence is exactly \(3.14737...\exp(-(T-298.0016...)^2)\).
Notably, this requires an \(\exp(\text{quadratic in }T)\) factor; candidates mostly have \(\exp(T\cdot c)\) or \(\exp(c/T)\), which cannot equal \(\exp(-(T-a)^2)\) on any continuous interval unless the Gaussian term is forced to vanish (but GT’s Gaussian term is nonzero for \(\epsilon\neq 0\)).

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.6057*(T - 298.00) + epsilon*3.1474*exp(-(T - 298.00)²)`

This simplifies to:
- A linear term in T: `-0.6057*T + 0.6057*298.00`
- A term: `epsilon * 3.1474 * exp(-(T-298)²)`

The key feature is the `epsilon * exp(-(T-298)²)` term - this is a Gaussian in T multiplied by epsilon. Let me check which candidates could produce this structure.

The GT has:
1. Linear in T (no epsilon dependence)
2. A constant term
3. `epsilon * exp(-T² + 596*T - 298²)` = `epsilon * exp(-T²) * exp(596T) * exp(-298²)`

This means I need a term like `epsilon * exp(quadratic in T)` or equivalently something that produces a Gaussian in T times epsilon.

Let me examine candidates for terms that could produce `epsilon * exp(f(T))`:

None of the candidates contain `exp(-T²)` or `exp(T²)` terms. The exponential terms in candidates are of the form `exp(T*c)` (linear in T in the exponent), not quadratic. The GT requires `exp(-(T-298)²)` which has a **quadratic** dependence on T in the exponent.

Terms like `exp(T*c)` can never equal `exp(-T²)` for all T - these are fundamentally different basis functions.

Let me check if any candidate has a structure that could produce a quadratic in T inside an exponential:

- Most candidates have `exp(T*c)` - linear in T
- Candidate 22: `exp(T*c3)*exp(c4*epsilon)` - still linear in T
- Candidate 25: `exp(T*c4)` inside log, and `exp(c8/T)` - neither quadratic
- Candidate 30: `exp(T*c5 + c6*epsilon)` inside log - linear in T
- Candidate 37: `cos(T*c8 + c9*epsilon)²` inside log - not Gaussian
- Candidate 38: `sin(...)³` - trigonometric, not Gaussian

**No candidate has `exp(-T²)` or any quadratic-in-T exponent.** The GT's Gaussian `exp(-(T-298)²)` cannot be reproduced by any of these candidates since they all use `exp(linear in T)`, polynomial, trigonometric, or logarithmic functions of T.

Since `exp(-T²)` is linearly independent from `exp(aT)`, polynomials in T, `cos(T)`, `sin(T)`, `log(T)`, `1/T`, etc., none of these candidates can match the GT.

Let me verify each candidate systematically - all have the wrong functional form for the T-dependent coupling with epsilon. None can produce the Gaussian `exp(-(T-298)²)`.
